Second Rational Objection: Past-Tense Reports in the Quran Imply Temporality
Razi presents the second rational objection that Quranic past-tense reports cannot be eternal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second rational objection against the eternity of the Quran based on past-tense verses, and why it poses a logical problem for those who hold the Quran to be eternal.

Core Idea
Past-tense Quranic verses force a dilemma: eternal speech cannot refer to a past event without contradiction.

This lesson presents the second rational objection raised by theologians against the doctrine of the Quran's eternity. It focuses on verses that use the past tense, such as 'We sent Noah' and 'We sent it down'. The argument is that if such verses were eternal, God would be speaking in pre-eternity about events that had not yet occurred, leading to absurdities. Let's examine the objection closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the examples of past-tense verses and the logical structure of the objection.
The objection uses three Quranic verses as examples.
2
Understand the dilemma
Identify the two impossible consequences: either pre-eternity is preceded (contradiction) or God's speech is false (impossible).
Both consequences are considered impossible (muhal).
3
Consider the conclusion
The objection concludes that the Quran cannot be eternal; it must be created in time.
This is an objection, not a final refutation.
4
Reflect on the assumption
Think about why defenders of eternity might reject this objection. They argue that God's speech is timeless, not spoken at a single instant.
The objection assumes a temporal framework for God's speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثانية : أنه أخبر بلفظ الماضي في مواضع كثيرة من القرآن كقوله: ﴿إِنَّا أَرْسَلْنَا نُوحًا﴾ [نوح: ١] و﴿إِنَّا أَنزَلْنَاهُ فِي لَيْلَةِ الْقَدْرِ﴾ [القدر: ١] و﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْهِمْ أَأَنذَرْتَهُمْ أَمْ لَمْ تُنذِرْهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ﴾ [البقرة: ٦] فلو كان هذا الإخبار قديما أزليّا لكان قد أخبر في الأزل عن شيء مضى، وهذا يقتضي أن يكون الأزل مسبوقا بغيره، وأن يكون كلام الله تعالى كذباً، ولما كان كل واحد منهما محالا علمنا أن هذا الإخبار يمتنع كونه أزليا.
The second objection: That He informed with the past tense in many places of the Qur'an, such as His statement: 'Indeed, We sent Noah' [Nuh 71:1] and 'Indeed, We sent it down on the Night of Decree' [Al-Qadr 97:1] and 'Indeed, those who disbelieve – it is all the same for them whether you warn them or do not warn them – they will not believe' [Al-Baqarah 2:6]. So if this informing were eternal and pre-eternal, then He would have informed in pre-eternity about something that had passed, and this would require that pre-eternity be preceded by something else, and that the speech of Allah Almighty be false. Since each of these is impossible, we know that this informing cannot be eternal.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents the second rational objection (shubhah aqliyya) against the eternity of the Quran. The objection focuses on the many verses in the Quran that use the past tense (fi'l madi), such as 'We sent Noah' (inna arsalna Nuhan) and 'We sent it down' (inna anzalnahu). If the Quranic speech is eternal (qadim azali), then these statements would have been uttered in pre-eternity—before the events described had occurred. This would mean that pre-eternity (al-azal) is preceded by something (since the event is past relative to the utterance), which is impossible because pre-eternity has no beginning. Alternatively, the statements would be false at the time of utterance, which contradicts God's truthfulness. Both consequences are impossible, so the Quran cannot be eternal. This objection is presented without immediate refutation, as it is part of the list of rational objections.

لفظ الماضي
أزلي

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that eternal speech would be uttered at a single instant in pre-eternity, as if God speaks in time.
Correction: Defenders of eternity argue that God's speech is timeless; it does not occur at a specific moment, so the objection's temporal assumptions are invalid.

Checkpoint
What does the second rational objection conclude about Quranic past-tense reports?
A) They are metaphorical and not literal
B) They prove the Quran is created because they refer to past events
C) They show that pre-eternity is temporal
D) They are eternal but reveal future events in past form

Key Takeaway
The second objection argues that because many Quranic verses use the past tense to refer to events that occurred after pre-eternity, those verses cannot be eternal without implying a contradiction or falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Impossibility of a Pre-Eternal Command: Razi's Refutation
Razi refutes the analogy of prophetic command to show pre-eternal command is impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why a pre-eternal command (amr azali) directed at future beings is rationally impossible according to Imam Razi.

Core Idea
A command requires an existing addressee; intention can precede, but not the request itself.

Imam Razi addresses a key objection to the doctrine that divine command is temporal, not pre-eternal. The objector draws analogies from God's eternal power and the Prophet's commands applying to future generations. Razi's answer hinges on a precise definition of command as a request (talab) and a careful analysis of the Prophet's words as information (ikhbar) rather than direct command. This lesson unpacks his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the first part of the passage where the objector presents two analogies: God's eternal power and the Prophet's commands continuing after his death. Notice the reasoning that command can precede its object.
The objector assumes command is like power—a non-relational attribute.
2
Identify Razi's key distinction
Focus on Razi's definition of command (amr) as a request (talab). He argues that a request without an existing addressee is inconceivable. Contrast this with 'intention to request' (azm) which can come before the addressee exists.
This distinction is the core of his refutation.
3
Analyze the Prophet example
Read Razi's analysis of the Prophet's commands. He reinterprets them as information (ikhbar) about future obligations, not as direct commands to non-existent persons. Note the role of listeners present to transmit the message.
The existence of an audience for transmission is crucial.
4
Synthesize the argument
Combine the two parts of Razi's answer to see why pre-eternal command is impossible. Without an addressee or audience, neither request nor information can occur. Thus the analogy fails.
The objection conflates God's eternal will with temporal command.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا يقال: لو لا يجوز أن يقال : عن ذلك الأمر الأزلي كان أمرًا في الأزل للأشخاص الذين سيوجدون في لا يزال كما أنه تعالى كان قادرًا في الأزل على أن يوجد الخلق في لا يزال؟ وأيضًا أليس أن النبي كان يأمر وينهى حال حياته كل من سيوجد بعده إلى قيام القيامة، فثبت أن تقدم الأمر على المأمور غير ممتنع. لأنا نقول : الأمر عبارة عن الطلب وتحقيق وجود الطلب مع أنه ليس هناك يطلب منه شيء محال في العقول، بل العزم على الطلب قد يتقدم على الطلب، مثل أن الواحد منا إذا علم أنه سيوجد له ولد فإنه في الحال يعزم على أنه إذا وجد له ذلك الولد، فبعد وجوده يطلب منه تحصيل العلم والأدب، فأما أن يقال: إنه قبل وجود الولد يطلب منه تحصيل العلم والأدب، فهذا البتة غير معقول. وأما أن قوله بأن النبي الله كان يأمر حال حياته وينهى كل من يوجد بعده إلى قيام القيامة فنقول : هذه مغالطة، وذلك لأن النبي الله ما كان له أمر ونهي على الخلق، بل هو له وكان يخبرنا أن أولئك الذين سيوجدون بعدي يحدث الله عليهم وجودهم وكمال عقلهم أنواعا من الأمر والنهي، وذلك الإخبار إنما حسن من الرسول لأنه حضر هناك من يسمع ذلك الخبر ويبلغه إلى الذين سيوجدون بعد ذلك، أما في الأزل فليس هناك أحد البتة يسمع ذلك الخبر، ويبلغه إلى الذين سيوجدون بعد ذلك، فظهر أن هذا المثال مغالطة محضة.
It may not be said: why is it not permissible to say that that pre-eternal command was a command in pre-eternity for the persons who will come into existence in the never-ending future, just as He—exalted—was powerful in pre-eternity to create creation in the never-ending future? And also, did not the Prophet command and prohibit during his life everyone who will come after him until the Day of Resurrection? So it is established that the precedence of the command over the commanded is not impossible. We say: command is an expression of a request, and the actual existence of a request when there is no one from whom to request something is impossible in intellects; rather, the intention to request may precede the request, like when one of us knows that a child will be born for him, then he immediately intends that when that child is born, after its existence he will request from it the acquisition of knowledge and good manners. But as for saying that before the child's existence he requests from it the acquisition of knowledge and good manners—this is absolutely unintelligible. As for the statement that the Prophet of God (ﷺ) used to command and prohibit during his life everyone who will come after him until the Day of Resurrection, we say: this is a fallacy, because the Prophet of God (ﷺ) had no command or prohibition over [future] creation; rather, he would inform us that those who will come after me—God will create for them upon their existence and the perfection of their intellect types of command and prohibition. That informing was only good from the Messenger because there were present those who heard that report and conveyed it to those who would come after. But in pre-eternity there is absolutely no one to hear that report and convey it to those who will come after. So it became clear that this analogy is a pure fallacy.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (shubhah wa jawab) concerning the possibility of a pre-eternal command directed at future beings. The objector argues: just as God's power was eternal though its effect (creation) occurs in time, why cannot His command be eternal though its object (the commanded action) occurs in time? Similarly, the Prophet's commands during his life applied to future people until Judgment Day, so command can precede its object. Razi's answer first distinguishes between 'request' (talab) and 'intention to request' (al-azm 'ala al-talab). 'Command' (amr) in the proper sense is an actual request, which requires an addressee who exists at the time of the request. Without an addressee, it is inconceivable. The objector's example of the Prophet is a fallacy: the Prophet did not directly command future people; he informed his contemporaries of future obligations, and that information was valid because there were listeners present to transmit it. In pre-eternity, there is no audience. Thus the analogy fails; the objector has conflated the eternal attribute of will/intention with the temporal act of commanding.

Key Terms
أمر
طلب
عزم
إخبار
مغالطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that since God's power is eternal, His command must also be eternal in the same way.
Correction: Razi shows that command is a relational attribute (requiring an existing addressee), unlike power which is a non-relational attribute of God.

Checkpoint
Why does Razi reject the analogy of the Prophet's command continuing after his death as a proof for a pre-eternal command?
A) Because the Prophet's command was not valid after his death.
B) Because the Prophet only informed about future commands, not directly commanded future people, and there were listeners present to transmit.
C) Because the Prophet's command was only for his own time.
D) Because future people are not morally responsible until they exist.

Key Takeaway
A command is a request that requires an existent addressee; thus a pre-eternal command to non-existent beings is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a, do you truly believe you are addressing the Living God who hears, or do you sometimes speak empty words as if no one is listening? How will you cultivate the conviction that your request reaches an actual Hearing Ear?
?
The objector confused his intention with an actual command. Where in your relationships have you assumed your good intentions exempt you from the duty to communicate clearly and at the right time? Confess one specific instance and plan to make it right.
?
The Prophet waited for the right audience before conveying obligations. Are there truths you are impatient to speak, forgetting that wisdom requires timing and readiness? Ask Allah to teach you to wait for His command before you speak.

The Second Objection Against Pre-Eternity: Past-Tense Verses
Objection that past-tense verses disprove pre-eternity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the presence of past-tense verbs in the Qur'an poses a logical problem for the claim that the Qur'an is pre-eternal.

Core Idea
Past-tense verses cannot be pre-eternal without making God's speech false or time incoherent.

In this lesson, we examine a powerful objection raised by those who argue that the Qur'an must be created. The objection focuses on verses that use the past tense—such as 'We sent Noah'—and argues that if the Qur'an were eternal, those statements would be false or imply that eternity is preceded by something else. Let's see how the objection is constructed step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic text of the objection carefully. Note the three Quranic examples given.
2
Identify the logical structure
The objection uses a conditional argument: If speech is eternal, then past-tense verses imply falsehood or a temporal sequence. Identify the two impossibilities derived.
3
Understand the conclusion
Since both implications are impossible, the premise that the speech is eternal must be false. This is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثانية : أنه أخبر بلفظ الماضي في مواضع كثيرة من القرآن كقوله: وَإِنَّا أَرْسَلْنَا نُوحًا [نوح: ١] وقوله: إِنَّا أَنزَلْنَاهُ فِي لَيْلَةِ الْقَدْرِ [القدر: ١] وقوله: إِنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْهِمْ أَوَأَنذَرْتَهُمْ أَمْ لَمْ تُنذِرْهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ [البقرة: ٦] فلو كان هذا الإخبار قديما أزليا لكان قد أخبر في الأزل عن شيء مضى، وهذا يقتضي أن يكون الأزل مسبوقا بغيره، وأن يكون كلام الله تعالى كذبا، ولما كان كل واحد منهما محالا علمنا أن هذا الإخبار يمتنع كونه أزليا. والجواب : أما جميع الشبه السمعية : فالجواب عنها شيء واحد وهو أن تصرف كل تلك الوجوه إلى هذه الحروف والأصوات، فإنا معترفون بأنها محدثة، وعندهم القرآن ليس إلا ما تركب عن هذه الحروف والأصوات، فكانت الدلائل التي ذكروها دالة على حدوث هذه الحروف والأصوات، ونحن لا ننازع في ذلك، وإنما ندعي قدم القرآن، لمعنى آخر، فكانت كل هذه الشبه ساقطة عن محل النزاع.
The second objection: that He informed using the past tense in many places of the Qur'an, such as His saying: 'And indeed We sent Noah' (71:1) and His saying: 'Indeed We sent it down on the Night of Decree' (97:1) and His saying: 'Indeed those who disbelieve—it is the same to them whether you warn them or do not warn them—they will not believe' (2:6). If this information were pre-eternal, then He would have informed in pre-eternity about something that had passed, and this would require that pre-eternity be preceded by something else, and that the speech of God be false. Since each of these is impossible, we know that this information cannot be pre-eternal. The answer: as for all the transmitted (sam'iyyah) objections, the answer for them is one thing: that all those aspects are to be referred to these letters and sounds, for we acknowledge that they are created. According to them (the opponents), the Qur'an is nothing but what is composed of these letters and sounds, so the proofs they mentioned only prove the temporal origination of these letters and sounds. We do not dispute that; we only claim the pre-eternity of the Qur'an in another sense. So all these objections miss the point of contention.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection (shubhah) against the pre-eternity of the Qur'an and the general response to all transmitted (sam'iyyah) objections. The objector argues: the Qur'an contains verses in the past tense (e.g., 'We sent Noah'), which would be false if the speech were pre-eternal because it would report an event before it occurred, making the speech a lie and implying pre-eternity is preceded. Therefore the Qur'an must be created. Razi's answer is that these objections actually target the created letters and sounds (al-huruf wa al-aswat), which we admit are created. The real dispute is about the eternal meaning (al-qadim al-nafsi), which is not composed of letters. Thus, the objections are irrelevant to the actual point of contention (mahall al-niza').

Key Terms
إخبار
لفظ الماضي
أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that the objection proves the entire Qur'an is created without distinction.
Correction: Razi later shows that the objection only applies to the temporal letters and sounds, not to the eternal meaning.

Checkpoint
What is the core logical problem with past-tense verses being pre-eternal?
A) The verses contain historical inaccuracies.
B) Pre-eternity cannot contain a report about a past event without implying a precedent or falsehood.
C) The past tense is grammatically incorrect.
D) The verses contradict other Quranic statements.

Key Takeaway
Past-tense verses in the Qur'an cannot be pre-eternal because that would entail either a contradiction in the concept of eternity or falsehood in God's speech.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read past-tense verses in the Quran like 'We sent Noah', do you ever feel a tension between the eternal nature of God's speech and the temporal events they describe? How does this objection force you to clarify your understanding of God's attributes, and what personal step will you take to resolve any doubt?
?
The reductio argues that pre-eternity cannot be preceded. Does this argument expose any inconsistency in your own beliefs about God and time? If so, what action will you take—will you diligently study the scholarly responses from Razi and others, or will you simply accept the limitation of your mind? Your commitment to truth is at stake.

Razi's Unified Response: Referring to Letters and Sounds
General answer to all scriptural objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's general strategy for deflecting all scriptural objections against the pre-eternity of the Qur'an.

Core Idea
All transmitted objections target the created letters and sounds, not the eternal speech.

After presenting the objection from past-tense verses, Imam Razi offers a sweeping response that applies not just to this objection but to all 'sam'iyyah' (transmitted) objections. The key move is to distinguish between the eternal attribute of speech (al-kalam al-nafsi) and its temporal expressions in letters and sounds. He argues that the opponents have conflated the two, and that their proofs only demonstrate the temporality of the latter, which we admit. Let's see how this argument works.

Guided Path
1
Read the general answer
Read the Arabic text of the answer. Notice how Razi introduces it as a unified response to all transmitted objections.
2
Identify the distinction
Razi distinguishes between the external letters/sounds and the inner speech. The opponents' arguments apply only to the former.
3
Recognize the concession
Razi concedes that the letters and sounds are created. The real dispute is about something else (the eternal meaning).
4
Understand the conclusion
Therefore, the objections miss the point (mahall al-niza') and do not refute the pre-eternity of the Qur'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثانية : أنه أخبر بلفظ الماضي في مواضع كثيرة من القرآن كقوله: وَإِنَّا أَرْسَلْنَا نُوحًا [نوح: ١] وقوله: إِنَّا أَنزَلْنَاهُ فِي لَيْلَةِ الْقَدْرِ [القدر: ١] وقوله: إِنَّ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا سَوَاءٌ عَلَيْهِمْ أَوَأَنذَرْتَهُمْ أَمْ لَمْ تُنذِرْهُمْ لَا يُؤْمِنُونَ [البقرة: ٦] فلو كان هذا الإخبار قديما أزليا لكان قد أخبر في الأزل عن شيء مضى، وهذا يقتضي أن يكون الأزل مسبوقا بغيره، وأن يكون كلام الله تعالى كذبا، ولما كان كل واحد منهما محالا علمنا أن هذا الإخبار يمتنع كونه أزليا. والجواب : أما جميع الشبه السمعية : فالجواب عنها شيء واحد وهو أن تصرف كل تلك الوجوه إلى هذه الحروف والأصوات، فإنا معترفون بأنها محدثة، وعندهم القرآن ليس إلا ما تركب عن هذه الحروف والأصوات، فكانت الدلائل التي ذكروها دالة على حدوث هذه الحروف والأصوات، ونحن لا ننازع في ذلك، وإنما ندعي قدم القرآن، لمعنى آخر، فكانت كل هذه الشبه ساقطة عن محل النزاع.
The second objection: that He informed using the past tense in many places of the Qur'an, such as His saying: 'And indeed We sent Noah' (71:1) and His saying: 'Indeed We sent it down on the Night of Decree' (97:1) and His saying: 'Indeed those who disbelieve—it is the same to them whether you warn them or do not warn them—they will not believe' (2:6). If this information were pre-eternal, then He would have informed in pre-eternity about something that had passed, and this would require that pre-eternity be preceded by something else, and that the speech of God be false. Since each of these is impossible, we know that this information cannot be pre-eternal. The answer: as for all the transmitted (sam'iyyah) objections, the answer for them is one thing: that all those aspects are to be referred to these letters and sounds, for we acknowledge that they are created. According to them (the opponents), the Qur'an is nothing but what is composed of these letters and sounds, so the proofs they mentioned only prove the temporal origination of these letters and sounds. We do not dispute that; we only claim the pre-eternity of the Qur'an in another sense. So all these objections miss the point of contention.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection (shubhah) against the pre-eternity of the Qur'an and the general response to all transmitted (sam'iyyah) objections. The objector argues: the Qur'an contains verses in the past tense (e.g., 'We sent Noah'), which would be false if the speech were pre-eternal because it would report an event before it occurred, making the speech a lie and implying pre-eternity is preceded. Therefore the Qur'an must be created. Razi's answer is that these objections actually target the created letters and sounds (al-huruf wa al-aswat), which we admit are created. The real dispute is about the eternal meaning (al-qadim al-nafsi), which is not composed of letters. Thus, the objections are irrelevant to the actual point of contention (mahall al-niza').

Key Terms
حروف وأصوات
محل النزاع
شبه سمعية

C) The meaning of the Qur'an
D) The inimitability of the Qur'an

Key Takeaway
All scriptural objections against the pre-eternity of the Qur'an are neutralised by referring them to the created letters and sounds, which we affirm are temporal.

Razi points out that the opponents missed the point because they reduced the Qur'an to its physical form. What practical step can you take today to realign your focus?
?
Razi conceded the creation of letters and sounds without dispute. Does the idea that the mushaf in your hands is created in its physical form ever unsettle your reverence for the Qur'an? How can embracing this distinction deepen—rather than weaken—your awe for Allah's eternal speech?

The Third Objection: An Eternal Command Would Never Cease
Razi presents the third objection that an eternal command would remain forever, using the example of Zayd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the permanence of a pre-eternal command is considered a rational problem and how it challenges the orthodox view of the Qur'an's eternity.

Core Idea
If the Qur'an is eternal, its commands would never expire, contradicting common sense.

After addressing two earlier rational objections, Razi now turns to a third: if Allah's speech is pre-eternal, then every command in it would remain perpetually binding, even after the commanded act is done. This seems to conflict with the obvious fact that commands cease to apply once fulfilled. In this lesson, we explore this objection and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Notice how Razi presents the objection as a conditional argument.
The objection uses the example of a command to pray to Zayd.
2
Identify the key premise
Identify the premise: what is pre-eternal cannot cease to exist. This is the logical foundation of the objection.
The objection assumes that commands are identical to the eternal attribute of speech.
3
Understand the example of Zayd
Razi illustrates with a command to Zayd to pray the morning prayer. If the command is eternal, it would remain after Zayd prays, after he dies, and after the Resurrection.
This shows the absurdity of an eternal command.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The objection concludes that since the command ceases, it must be originated (hadith), not pre-eternal.
This directly challenges the Ash'ari doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الثالثة : أن كلام الله تعالى لو كان قديما أزليا لكان باقيا أبديا؛ لأن ما يمتنع عدمه فيكون قوله تعالى لزيد صل، باقيا بعد أن صلي زيد صلاة الصبح وبعد أن مات وبعد أن قامت القيامة، وهكذا يكون باقيا أبد الآباد ودهر الداهرين، ومعلوم أن ذلك على خلاف المعقول ؛ فإنه تعالى إذا أمر عبده بفعل من الأفعال فإذا أتى ذلك العبد بذلك الفعل لم يبق ذلك الأمر متوجها عليه، وإذا ثبت أن ذلك الأمر قد زال ثبت أنه كان محدثا لا قديما. الشبهة الرابعة : أجمعت الأمة على أن النسخ حق، والنسخ عبارة إما عن ارتفاع الحكم بعد ثبوته وإما عند انتهائه، وأيا ما كان فهو يقتضي زوال ذلك الأمر، وذلك الخطاب بعد ثبوته وكل ما زال بعد ثبوته لم يكن قديما ؛ لأن ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه. والجواب عن الشبهة الثالثة والرابعة : هو أن قدرته تعالى كانت متعلقة
The third objection: that if the speech of God were pre-eternal, it would remain eternal forever; because what is impossible of non-existence—so His statement to Zayd 'Pray' would remain after Zayd had prayed the morning prayer, after he died, after the Resurrection, and thus remain forever and ever. It is known that this is contrary to reason; for when He commands His servant to do an action, and that servant performs that action, the command no longer applies to him. If it is established that the command has ceased, it is established that it was originated, not pre-eternal. The fourth objection: the community has agreed that abrogation (naskh) is valid. Abrogation is either the removal of a ruling after its establishment or its end. Either way, it entails the cessation of that command and address after its establishment. Whatever ceases after establishment cannot be pre-eternal, because what is pre-eternal is impossible to cease. The answer to the third and fourth objections: that His power was related...
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage presents the third and fourth objections and their combined answer. The third objection argues that an eternal command would continue forever, even after the commanded act is done, which is absurd. The fourth objection invokes consensus on abrogation (naskh): abrogated rulings cease, so they cannot be eternal. Razi's answer begins but is cut off: 'that His power was related...' (anna qudratahu ta'ala kanat muta'alliqa). The full answer is not in this window, but it likely parallels his response to the first rational objection, using the analogy of eternal power that becomes related to temporal acts without change in the attribute itself. The incomplete sentence suggests he is applying the same principle: the eternal attribute of speech relates to temporal objects (commands, prohibitions) without undergoing change or cessation in its essence.

أزلي
زوال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that an eternal command cannot cease because it is an eternal attribute itself.
Correction: Razi's argument highlights that the cessation of the command does not necessarily mean the attribute ceases; but the objection is that the specific command itself would have to remain, which is absurd.

The Fourth Objection: Abrogation Implies Change in the Eternal
Razi presents the fourth objection based on abrogation and begins the combined answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consensus on abrogation is used to argue against the pre-eternity of the Qur'an, and how Razi starts his response.

Core Idea
If abrogation is possible, then commands change, so they cannot be eternal.

The fourth objection appeals to the universally accepted practice of abrogation (naskh) in Islamic law. If the Qur'an contains abrogated verses, then the commands within it have ceased to apply. This seems to contradict the idea that they are pre-eternal, since eternal things cannot cease. Razi's response, though incomplete here, begins by hinting at the distinction between the eternal attribute and its temporal relations.

The Fourth Objection: Abrogation and the Eternity of Speech
The fourth rational objection against the eternity of divine speech and its answer using the analogy of power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth rational objection against the eternity of God's speech based on abrogation and how Imam al-Razi answers it using the analogy of divine power.

Core Idea
Abrogation does not disprove the eternity of speech because the attribute can cease to relate without ceasing to exist.

The fourth objection argues that since rulings can be abrogated, God's command must be temporal. Imam al-Razi responds by drawing an analogy with divine power, which is eternal yet its relation to creation changes. Let's examine the objection and its sophisticated answer.

Guided Path
1
Read the fourth objection
Read the Arabic passage for the fourth objection and its translation. Notice the logical steps: consensus on abrogation → cessation of command → impossibility of eternity.
2
Understand the objection's premise
Abrogation (naskh) involves the removal of a ruling. If the ruling was commanded by eternal speech, it could not be removed. Therefore, speech must be temporal.
The objection assumes that the command itself is the eternal speech.
3
Read the answer
Read the answer where Imam al-Razi uses the analogy of divine power. Power is an eternal attribute that was related to bringing the world into existence, but when the world was created, that relation ceased without the attribute becoming temporal.
4
Reflect on the analogy
Consider how the analogy resolves the objection. The key point is that an eternal attribute can have a temporal relation to its object. Similarly, the eternal attribute of speech can cease to relate to a particular command without itself changing.
This preserves the eternity of the attribute while acknowledging the temporality of its specific manifestations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الرابعة : أجمعت الأمة على أن النسخ حق، والنسخ عبارة إما عن ارتفاع الحكم بعد ثبوته وإما عند انتهائه، وأيا ما كان فهو يقتضي زوال ذلك الأمر، وذلك الخطاب بعد ثبوته وكل ما زال بعد ثبوته لم يكن قديمًا ; لأن ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه.
الشبهة الخامسة : لو كان كلام الله تعالى قديمًا أزليّا لكان تعلقه بمتعلقاته ثابتا له لذاته، ولو كان كذلك لكان عام التعلق بكل ما يصح تعلقه به ولما كان من مذهبكم أن الحسن والقبح لا يثبتان إلا بالشرع فإذن كل ما كان مأمورًا لا يمتنع أن يكون منهياً، وكل ما كان منهيًا لا يمتنع أن يكون مأمورًا ، فيلزم تعلق أمر الله تعالى بجميع الأشياء، وتعلق نهيه بجميعها، ويلزم أن تكون جميع الأشياء مأمورة منهية حسنة قبيحة، وكل ذلك محال، فثبت أن كلام الله يمتنع أن يكون أزليّا.
والجواب : أما جميع الشبه السمعية : فالجواب عنها شيء واحد وهو أن تصرف كل تلك الوجوه إلى هذه الحروف والأصوات، فإنا معترفون بأنها محدثة، وعندهم القرآن ليس إلا ما تركب عن هذه الحروف والأصوات، فكانت الدلائل التي ذكروها دالة على حدوث هذه الحروف والأصوات، ونحن لا ننازع في ذلك، وإنما ندعي قدم القرآن، لمعنى آخر، فكانت كل هذه الشبه ساقطة عن محل النزاع. وأما الجواب عن الشبه العقلية : فالجواب عن الشبهة الأولى : هو أنها معارضة بالقدرة ; فإنها صفة تقتضي صحة الفعل، ثم إنها كانت ثابتة في الأزل مع أن الفعل كان ممتنعا، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال : الأمر عبارة عن الصفة المقتضية لطلب الفعل، ثم إنها كانت في الأزل مع أن طلب الفعل كان في الأزل محالاً؟ والجواب عن الشبهة الثانية أنه تعالى كان عالما في الأزل بأنه سيخلق العالم، ثم لما خلقه في الأزل صار العلم بأنه قد خلقه في الماضي، ولما لم يقتض هذا حدوث هذا العالم وتغيره، فكذا في الخبر. والجواب عن الشبهة الثالثة والرابعة : هو أن قدرته تعالى كانت متعلقة من الأزل إلى الأبد بإيجاد العالم، ولما أوجد العالم لم يبق ذلك التعلق ; لأن إيجاد الموجود محال ولما زال هذا التعلق ولم يقتض ذلك حدوث قدرة الله تعالى، فكذا القول في الكلام. والجواب عن الشبهة الخامسة : أن قدرة الله تعالى لها صلاحية التعلق بإيجاد كل الممكنات، ثم إنها تعلقت بإيجاد البعض دون البعض مع أن هذه القدرة قديمة، وإذا عقل ذلك في القدرة فلم لا يعقل مثله في الكلام ؟ فهذه جملة الكلام في هذه المسألة.
The Fourth Objection: The community has agreed that abrogation (al-naskh) is true, and abrogation is either the removal of a ruling after its establishment or at its termination, and whichever it is, it necessitates the cessation of that command and that address after its establishment, and everything that ceases after its establishment was not eternal, because what is established as eternal its non-existence is impossible. The Fifth Objection: If the speech of God Most High were eternal and pre-eternal, then its relation to its objects would be established for It by Its essence, and if so, It would be universal in relation to everything to which It can relate, and since it is your doctrine that good and evil (al-husn wa al-qubh) are only established by revelation, then everything that is commanded is not impossible to be prohibited, and everything that is prohibited is not impossible to be commanded; thus it follows that God's command relates to all things and His prohibition relates to all things, and it follows that all things are commanded, prohibited, good, and evil, and all that is impossible; so it is established that God's speech cannot be eternal. The Answer: As for all the scriptural objections (al-shubah al-sam'iyya), the answer to them is one thing: that all those aspects refer to these letters and sounds; we acknowledge that they are created (muhdatha), and according to them (the opponents) the Qur'an is nothing but what is composed of these letters and sounds; so the evidences they mentioned indicate the createdness of these letters and sounds, and we do not dispute that; rather we claim the eternity of the Qur'an for another meaning; so all these objections fall away from the point of dispute. As for the answer to the rational objections (al-shubah al-'aqliyya): The answer to the first objection is that it is countered by power (al-qudra); for it is an attribute that entails the possibility of the act, but it was established in pre-eternity while the act was impossible; so why is it not permissible to say that command is an expression of the attribute that entails the demand for the act, and then it existed in pre-eternity while the demand for the act was impossible in pre-eternity? The answer to the second objection is that He Most High was knowing in pre-eternity that He would create the world, then when He created it in time, knowledge became that He had created it in the past, and since this did not necessitate the temporality of this world and its change, so likewise in the case of report (al-khabar). The answer to the third and fourth objections is that His power Most High was related from pre-eternity to eternity with bringing the world into existence, and when He brought the world into existence that relation did not remain, because bringing into existence that which exists is impossible; and when this relation ceased and that did not necessitate the temporality of God's power, so likewise the statement regarding speech. The answer to the fifth objection is that God's power has the potentiality to relate to bringing into existence all possible things, but then it related to bringing into existence some without others while this power is eternal; and if that is conceivable regarding power, then why is its like not conceivable regarding speech? This is the summary of the discourse on this issue.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents two more rational objections against the eternity of God's speech (the fourth and fifth) and then provides a unified response to all scriptural objections followed by specific responses to each rational objection, including the first three not shown in this window. The passage is structured as a series of objections and answers typical of kalam dialectic.

First, the fourth objection: The universal consensus on abrogation (naskh) proves that commands can cease to apply. If God's speech were eternal, it could not cease, because an eternal thing cannot undergo non-existence. Therefore, God's speech must be temporal (hadith). The fifth objection argues that if God's speech were eternal, its relation to its objects would be necessary and universal, leading to the absurdity that every action would be both commanded and prohibited, and good and evil simultaneously, since good and evil are only defined by revelation (shar'), not by reason. Therefore, God's speech cannot be eternal.

Then the response: First, for all scriptural objections, the answer is one: they all confuse the eternal attribute of speech with its temporal expression in letters and sounds. The Qur'an as composed of sounds and letters is created (muhdath), and the opponents' arguments only prove the temporality of that, not the eternal attribute itself. This removes the objections from the point of dispute.

Second, for the rational objections: The first objection (about command ceasing) is countered by analogy with divine power (qudra). Power is an eternal attribute that entails the possibility of an act, yet it existed in pre-eternity when the act was impossible; similarly, command is an attribute entailing demand, and it can exist in pre-eternity even though the demand was impossible. The second objection (about knowledge) is answered by noting that God's knowledge is eternal yet its content changes as events occur (future becomes past), without that implying change in the attribute itself; likewise, khabar (report) can be eternal but relate to temporal events. The third and fourth objections are answered together by analogy with divine power: God's power was eternally related to creating the world, but when the world was created, that relation ceased without implying temporality of the power; similarly, the relation of speech can cease without the speech itself being temporal. The fifth objection is answered by pointing out that God's power is eternal yet it relates to some possible things and not others; similarly, God's speech can be eternal yet relate to specific commands and prohibitions without being universal. Thus all objections are refuted.

The passage concludes with 'This is the summary of the discourse on this issue' (فهذه جملة الكلام في هذه المسألة).

Key Terms
النسخ
الأمر
القدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If an attribute's relation to its object changes, the attribute itself must change.
Correction: An eternal attribute can remain unchanged while its specific relations to temporal objects change, as seen with divine power: it is eternal yet its relation to the act of creation ceased after the world existed.

Checkpoint
What analogy does Imam al-Razi use to answer the fourth objection?
A) The analogy of God's knowledge, which is eternal yet its content changes.
B) The analogy of God's power, which was eternally related to creating the world, but that relation ceased without the power becoming temporal.
C) The analogy of human command, which ceases after the act is performed.
D) The analogy of the abrogation of rulings, which proves that commands can change.

Key Takeaway
The fourth objection is refuted by showing that an eternal attribute can cease to relate to a particular object without itself becoming temporal, using the analogy of divine power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt unsettled when learning that some Quranic verses are abrogated? Does the analogy of divine power help you trust that God's speech remains unchanged even when specific rulings change? How will you remind yourself of this distinction when you encounter abrogation in the future?
?
If God's power could be eternally related to creating the world without being temporal, can you accept the same for His speech? What does this imply about your confidence in the permanence of God's attributes, even when circumstances change?
?
The analogy in this lesson invites you to see abrogation not as a weakness but as a display of the richness of an eternal attribute. Will you let this understanding deepen your reverence for the Quran, even the parts that are no longer applied? What practical change does this call you to make in your attitude toward divine commands?

The Fifth Objection: Universality of Divine Command and Its Answer
The fifth rational objection against the eternity of divine speech and its answer using the selectivity of divine power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth rational objection that the eternity of speech would lead to all things being both commanded and prohibited, and how Imam al-Razi answers it by appealing to the selectivity of divine power.

Core Idea
The eternity of speech does not require universal command; just as power selects some possibilities, speech selects some commands.

The fifth objection argues that eternal speech would have to relate to all possible objects, causing logical absurdities. Imam al-Razi responds by noting that divine power is eternal yet only relates to some possible things, so speech can similarly be selective.

Guided Path
1
Read the fifth objection
Read the Arabic passage for the fifth objection and its translation. Notice the logical chain: if speech is eternal, its relation is necessary; if necessary, it must be universal; given Ash'ari ethics, all things would be commanded and prohibited, which is impossible.
2
Analyze the objection's assumption
The objection assumes that an eternal attribute must relate to all possible objects uniformly. Imam al-Razi will challenge this assumption.
3
Read the answer
Read the answer where the selectivity of divine power is used as an analogy. Power is eternal yet it relates to some possible things and not others; likewise, speech can be eternal yet relate to specific commands.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this answer preserves the eternity of speech while allowing for specific, non-universal commands. It shows that the objection falsely imposes a requirement that does not exist.
This answer also relates to the broader Ash'ari principle that God's attributes are not constrained by human expectations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الرابعة : أجمعت الأمة على أن النسخ حق، والنسخ عبارة إما عن ارتفاع الحكم بعد ثبوته وإما عند انتهائه، وأيا ما كان فهو يقتضي زوال ذلك الأمر، وذلك الخطاب بعد ثبوته وكل ما زال بعد ثبوته لم يكن قديمًا ; لأن ما ثبت قدمه استحال عدمه.
الشبهة الخامسة : لو كان كلام الله تعالى قديمًا أزليّا لكان تعلقه بمتعلقاته ثابتا له لذاته، ولو كان كذلك لكان عام التعلق بكل ما يصح تعلقه به ولما كان من مذهبكم أن الحسن والقبح لا يثبتان إلا بالشرع فإذن كل ما كان مأمورًا لا يمتنع أن يكون منهياً، وكل ما كان منهيًا لا يمتنع أن يكون مأمورًا ، فيلزم تعلق أمر الله تعالى بجميع الأشياء، وتعلق نهيه بجميعها، ويلزم أن تكون جميع الأشياء مأمورة منهية حسنة قبيحة، وكل ذلك محال، فثبت أن كلام الله يمتنع أن يكون أزليّا.
والجواب : أما جميع الشبه السمعية : فالجواب عنها شيء واحد وهو أن تصرف كل تلك الوجوه إلى هذه الحروف والأصوات، فإنا معترفون بأنها محدثة، وعندهم القرآن ليس إلا ما تركب عن هذه الحروف والأصوات، فكانت الدلائل التي ذكروها دالة على حدوث هذه الحروف والأصوات، ونحن لا ننازع في ذلك، وإنما ندعي قدم القرآن، لمعنى آخر، فكانت كل هذه الشبه ساقطة عن محل النزاع. وأما الجواب عن الشبه العقلية : فالجواب عن الشبهة الأولى : هو أنها معارضة بالقدرة ; فإنها صفة تقتضي صحة الفعل، ثم إنها كانت ثابتة في الأزل مع أن الفعل كان ممتنعا، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال : الأمر عبارة عن الصفة المقتضية لطلب الفعل، ثم إنها كانت في الأزل مع أن طلب الفعل كان في الأزل محالاً؟ والجواب عن الشبهة الثانية أنه تعالى كان عالما في الأزل بأنه سيخلق العالم، ثم لما خلقه في الأزل صار العلم بأنه قد خلقه في الماضي، ولما لم يقتض هذا حدوث هذا العالم وتغيره، فكذا في الخبر. والجواب عن الشبهة الثالثة والرابعة : هو أن قدرته تعالى كانت متعلقة من الأزل إلى الأبد بإيجاد العالم، ولما أوجد العالم لم يبق ذلك التعلق ; لأن إيجاد الموجود محال ولما زال هذا التعلق ولم يقتض ذلك حدوث قدرة الله تعالى، فكذا القول في الكلام. والجواب عن الشبهة الخامسة : أن قدرة الله تعالى لها صلاحية التعلق بإيجاد كل الممكنات، ثم إنها تعلقت بإيجاد البعض دون البعض مع أن هذه القدرة قديمة، وإذا عقل ذلك في القدرة فلم لا يعقل مثله في الكلام ؟ فهذه جملة الكلام في هذه المسألة.
The Fourth Objection: The community has agreed that abrogation (al-naskh) is true, and abrogation is either the removal of a ruling after its establishment or at its termination, and whichever it is, it necessitates the cessation of that command and that address after its establishment, and everything that ceases after its establishment was not eternal, because what is established as eternal its non-existence is impossible. The Fifth Objection: If the speech of God Most High were eternal and pre-eternal, then its relation to its objects would be established for It by Its essence, and if so, It would be universal in relation to everything to which It can relate, and since it is your doctrine that good and evil (al-husn wa al-qubh) are only established by revelation, then everything that is commanded is not impossible to be prohibited, and everything that is prohibited is not impossible to be commanded; thus it follows that God's command relates to all things and His prohibition relates to all things, and it follows that all things are commanded, prohibited, good, and evil, and all that is impossible; so it is established that God's speech cannot be eternal. The Answer: As for all the scriptural objections (al-shubah al-sam'iyya), the answer to them is one thing: that all those aspects refer to these letters and sounds; we acknowledge that they are created (muhdatha), and according to them (the opponents) the Qur'an is nothing but what is composed of these letters and sounds; so the evidences they mentioned indicate the createdness of these letters and sounds, and we do not dispute that; rather we claim the eternity of the Qur'an for another meaning; so all these objections fall away from the point of dispute. As for the answer to the rational objections (al-shubah al-'aqliyya): The answer to the first objection is that it is countered by power (al-qudra); for it is an attribute that entails the possibility of the act, but it was established in pre-eternity while the act was impossible; so why is it not permissible to say that command is an expression of the attribute that entails the demand for the act, and then it existed in pre-eternity while the demand for the act was impossible in pre-eternity? The answer to the second objection is that He Most High was knowing in pre-eternity that He would create the world, then when He created it in time, knowledge became that He had created it in the past, and since this did not necessitate the temporality of this world and its change, so likewise in the case of report (al-khabar). The answer to the third and fourth objections is that His power Most High was related from pre-eternity to eternity with bringing the world into existence, and when He brought the world into existence that relation did not remain, because bringing into existence that which exists is impossible; and when this relation ceased and that did not necessitate the temporality of God's power, so likewise the statement regarding speech. The answer to the fifth objection is that God's power has the potentiality to relate to bringing into existence all possible things, but then it related to bringing into existence some without others while this power is eternal; and if that is conceivable regarding power, then why is its like not conceivable regarding speech? This is the summary of the discourse on this issue.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage presents two more rational objections against the eternity of God's speech (the fourth and fifth) and then provides a unified response to all scriptural objections followed by specific responses to each rational objection, including the first three not shown in this window. The passage is structured as a series of objections and answers typical of kalam dialectic.

First, the fourth objection: The universal consensus on abrogation (naskh) proves that commands can cease to apply. If God's speech were eternal, it could not cease, because an eternal thing cannot undergo non-existence. Therefore, God's speech must be temporal (hadith). The fifth objection argues that if God's speech were eternal, its relation to its objects would be necessary and universal, leading to the absurdity that every action would be both commanded and prohibited, and good and evil simultaneously, since good and evil are only defined by revelation (shar'), not by reason. Therefore, God's speech cannot be eternal.

Then the response: First, for all scriptural objections, the answer is one: they all confuse the eternal attribute of speech with its temporal expression in letters and sounds. The Qur'an as composed of sounds and letters is created (muhdath), and the opponents' arguments only prove the temporality of that, not the eternal attribute itself. This removes the objections from the point of dispute.

Second, for the rational objections: The first objection (about command ceasing) is countered by analogy with divine power (qudra). Power is an eternal attribute that entails the possibility of an act, yet it existed in pre-eternity when the act was impossible; similarly, command is an attribute entailing demand, and it can exist in pre-eternity even though the demand was impossible. The second objection (about knowledge) is answered by noting that God's knowledge is eternal yet its content changes as events occur (future becomes past), without that implying change in the attribute itself; likewise, khabar (report) can be eternal but relate to temporal events. The third and fourth objections are answered together by analogy with divine power: God's power was eternally related to creating the world, but when the world was created, that relation ceased without implying temporality of the power; similarly, the relation of speech can cease without the speech itself being temporal. The fifth objection is answered by pointing out that God's power is eternal yet it relates to some possible things and not others; similarly, God's speech can be eternal yet relate to specific commands and prohibitions without being universal. Thus all objections are refuted.

The passage concludes with 'This is the summary of the discourse on this issue' (فهذه جملة الكلام في هذه المسألة).

The Analogy of Power and Speech
Razi answers the fifth doubt about God's speech by analogy with power.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi uses the analogy of God's eternal power to defend the eternality of God's speech.

Core Idea
Eternal attributes can relate to temporal things without being temporal themselves.

This short passage is the climax of a long discussion about God's speech. A doubt is raised: if God's speech commands temporal things, must it itself be temporal? Imam Razi answers by drawing a parallel with God's power, which is eternal yet brings about temporal creations. The logic is tight and elegant.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice how the answer is structured as an analogy: first premise about power, then application to speech.
The phrase 'Why should its like not be understood in speech?' is the key rhetorical move.
2
Identify the core analogy
Find the two terms being compared: God's power (qudra) and God's speech (kalam). Note the shared property: both are eternal attributes that relate to temporal things.
The analogy rests on the capacity (salahiyya) of an eternal attribute to attach to multiple possible objects at different times.
3
Understand the logical principle
The principle is that the eternal attribute's 'attachment' (ta'alluq) to a temporal effect does not make the attribute temporal. This refutes the doubt.
This is a standard kalam argument: parity of reasoning (tamthil).
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this matters: it preserves the eternity of God's speech (kalam nafsi) while allowing it to relate to temporal commands and prohibitions.
Without this answer, one might mistakenly think God's speech is created.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الشبهة الخامسة : أن قدرة الله تعالى لها صلاحية التعلق بإيجاد كل الممكنات، ثم إنها تعلقت بإيجاد البعض دون البعض مع أن هذه القدرة قديمة، وإذا عقل ذلك في القدرة فلم لا يعقل مثله في الكلام ؟ فهذه جملة الكلام في هذه المسألة.
And the answer to the fifth doubt: that the power of God the Exalted has the capacity to attach to bringing into existence all contingent things, then it attached to bringing into existence some without others despite this power being eternal. And if that is understood in power, why should its like not be understood in speech? So this is the summary of the discourse on this issue.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage presents the answer to a fifth doubt concerning the speech of God. The doubt likely questioned how God's speech could be eternal if it relates to temporal commands. Imam Razi argues by analogy with God's power: God's power is eternal yet it attaches to creating some things at specific times and not others. Similarly, God's speech (kalam) can be eternal even though it relates to temporal events. The reasoning is that the capacity (salahiyya) of an eternal attribute to relate to temporal objects does not imply that the attribute itself is temporal. Thus, the objection is refuted by parity of reasoning.

Defining Baqa' and the Two Positions
Imam Razi defines baqa' and presents two positions on its attribute status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of baqa' (eternity) and the two scholarly positions on whether it is an additional attribute to God's essence.

Core Idea
Baqa' is defined as existence after origination, but scholars disagree if it is a separate attribute.

Before we can discuss God's eternity (baqa'), we need a clear definition of the term and the key disagreement that divides theologians. Imam Razi begins by defining baqa' in relation to huduth (origination) and then presents the two main positions on whether baqa' is an attribute additional to God's essence. This foundational framing sets up the three investigations that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of baqa'
Read the Arabic passage starting from 'اعلم أن الشيء إذا كان معدوماً' to understand how Razi defines huduth and baqa'.
Notice that huduth is the first moment of existence, and baqa' is subsequent existence.
2
Identify the two positions
Find the two groups of scholars and their positions on whether baqa' is an additional attribute (sifa za'ida).
The first group says it is not additional; the second says it is additional.
3
Consider why this matters
Reflect on why the status of baqa' as an attribute matters for God's nature. This debate affects how we understand God's eternal existence.
If baqa' is additional, God's essence would have a distinct eternal quality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثامنة عشرة في بقاء الله تعالى والكلام فيه مرتب على فصلين : الفصل الأول : في حقيقة البقاء اعلم أن الشيء إذا كان معدوماً ثم صار موجودًا فوجوده في الزمان الأول هو الحدوث، ثم وجوده في الذي بعد ذلك هو البقاء. وأكثر المحققين اتفقوا على أن الحدوث لا يمكن أن يكون صفة زائدة على ذات الحادث، وأما البقاء فقد اختلفوا في أنه هل هو زائد على ذات الباقي أن لا؟ فذهب القاضي أبو بكر وإمام الحرمين - من أصحابنا - وجمهور معتزلة البصرة إلى أن كون الباقي باقيا ليس صفة زائدة على الذات وذهب الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري وأكثر أتباعه وجمهور معتزلة بغدادي إلى أنه صفة زائدة على الذات. واعلم أن في هذه المسألة أبحاثا ثلاثة : البحث الأول: أن استمرار الذات هل هو مفهوم زائد على الذات أم لا؟ في فقال قوم: إنه مفهوم زائد على الذات ؛ وذلك لأن الذات كانت حاصلة الزمان الأول، ولم يكن استمرار الذات حاصلا في الزمان الأول، فلما حصل في الزمان الثاني حصل الذات وحصل استمرار الذات وهذا يقتضي أن يكون استمرار الذات مغايرا لنفس الذات. وعلى هذا الكلام ،إشكال وهو أنه كلما صدق على الذات أنها صارت مستمرة بعد أن لم تكن كذلك صدق عليها أنها كانت متجددة في الزمان الأول ثم في الزمان الثاني صارت غير متجددة، فقد صارت غير متجددة بعد أن كانت موصوفة بأنها متجددة فيلزم أن يكون حدوثها وتجددها صفة زائدة على ذاتها، وهذا محال ؛ لأنه لو كان الحدوث صفة زائدة لكانت تلك الصفة حادثة، ويلزم التسلسل.
The eighteenth issue: On God's eternity (baqa'). The discourse on it is arranged in two chapters: The first chapter: On the reality of eternity. Know that a thing, when it was non-existent then came into existence, its existence in the first moment is origination (huduth), and then its existence after that is eternity (baqa'). Most of the verifiers agreed that origination cannot be an attribute additional to the essence of the originated. As for eternity, they differed as to whether it is additional to the essence of the eternal or not. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr and Imam al-Haramayn (from our companions) and the majority of the Basran Mu'tazila held that the thing's being eternal is not an attribute additional to the essence. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and most of his followers and the majority of the Baghdadi Mu'tazila held that it is an attribute additional to the essence. And know that in this issue there are three investigations: The first investigation: Whether the continuance of the essence is an additional concept to the essence or not? Some said: It is an additional concept to the essence; because the essence was present in the first moment, and the continuance of the essence did not exist in the first moment. When it came to be in the second moment, the essence came to be and the continuance of the essence came to be, and this necessitates that the continuance of the essence is other than the essence itself. But this statement has an objection: Whenever it is true of the essence that it has become continuous after not having been so, it is true of it that it was renewing (mutajaddid) in the first moment, then in the second moment it became non-renewing. So it became non-renewing after it was described as renewing. This necessitates that its origination and renewal (huduth and tajaddud) be attributes additional to its essence. And this is impossible; because if origination were an additional attribute, that attribute would be originated, leading to infinite regress.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage begins the eighteenth issue (mas'ala) of the work, on God's eternity (baqa'). The author announces that the discussion is organized into two chapters (fasl). The first chapter is on the reality of baqa'. Imam Razi defines huduth (origination) as the existence of a thing when it was non-existent, and baqa' (eternity/continuance) as its existence after that. He notes that scholars agreed that huduth is not an additional attribute (since it is the very fact of coming into existence, not a separate quality). However, they differed on baqa': is it an additional attribute or not? He lists two positions: the first group (Qadi Abu Bakr, Imam al-Haramayn from the Ash'aris, and most Basran Mu'tazila) says baqa' is not additional; the second group (Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, most of his followers, and most Baghdadi Mu'tazila) says it is additional. Then the author states that there are three investigations (abhath) in this issue. He presents the first investigation: whether the continuance (istimrar) of the essence is an additional concept. Some argue it is additional: in the first moment, the essence existed but its continuance did not; in the second moment, both exist, so continuance must be other than the essence. Then an objection (ishkal) is raised: if we say the essence 'became continuous' after not being continuous, then we must say it was 'renewing' (mutajaddid) in the first moment, and in the second moment it became 'non-renewing'. This would require that 'origination' and 'renewal' themselves are attributes additional to the essence, which is impossible because it would lead to infinite regress. The passage ends with this objection waiting for an answer.

Key Terms
بقاء
حدوث
صفة زائدة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think huduth (origination) is also an additional attribute, but the text explicitly states that scholars agreed it is not.
Correction: Huduth is simply the fact of coming into existence; it is not a separate attribute added to the essence.

D) It is identical to baqa'

Key Takeaway
The central debate around baqa' is whether it is an attribute additional to God's essence, with two main scholarly camps.

The First Investigation: Is Continuance an Additional Concept?
Imam Razi presents the first investigation on continuance as an additional concept with an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that continuance (istimrar) is an additional concept and the objection that leads to infinite regress.

Core Idea
Claiming continuance is additional leads to a regress involving origination itself.

After establishing the two positions on baqa', Razi presents the first of three investigations. Here he examines whether 'continuance' (istimrar) of the essence is an additional concept. Some argue yes, because the essence exists in the first moment without continuance, but in the second moment both exist. However, this argument is met with a powerful objection: it would force us to say that origination and renewal are also additional attributes, leading to an infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument for continuance being additional
Find the passage starting with 'فقال قوم: إنه مفهوم زائد على الذات' and understand their reasoning.
The argument uses the temporal difference between the first and second moments.
2
Follow the objection
Read the objection beginning with 'وعلى هذا الكلام إشكال' and see how it counters the argument.
The objection shows that the same logic would make huduth an additional attribute, leading to regress.
3
Identify the regress
Understand why infinite regress (tasalsul) would be impossible, especially in God's case.
The attribute of huduth would itself be originated, requiring another attribute, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثامنة عشرة في بقاء الله تعالى والكلام فيه مرتب على فصلين : الفصل الأول : في حقيقة البقاء اعلم أن الشيء إذا كان معدوماً ثم صار موجودًا فوجوده في الزمان الأول هو الحدوث، ثم وجوده في الذي بعد ذلك هو البقاء. وأكثر المحققين اتفقوا على أن الحدوث لا يمكن أن يكون صفة زائدة على ذات الحادث، وأما البقاء فقد اختلفوا في أنه هل هو زائد على ذات الباقي أن لا؟ فذهب القاضي أبو بكر وإمام الحرمين - من أصحابنا - وجمهور معتزلة البصرة إلى أن كون الباقي باقيا ليس صفة زائدة على الذات وذهب الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري وأكثر أتباعه وجمهور معتزلة بغدادي إلى أنه صفة زائدة على الذات. واعلم أن في هذه المسألة أبحاثا ثلاثة : البحث الأول: أن استمرار الذات هل هو مفهوم زائد على الذات أم لا؟ في فقال قوم: إنه مفهوم زائد على الذات ؛ وذلك لأن الذات كانت حاصلة الزمان الأول، ولم يكن استمرار الذات حاصلا في الزمان الأول، فلما حصل في الزمان الثاني حصل الذات وحصل استمرار الذات وهذا يقتضي أن يكون استمرار الذات مغايرا لنفس الذات. وعلى هذا الكلام ،إشكال وهو أنه كلما صدق على الذات أنها صارت مستمرة بعد أن لم تكن كذلك صدق عليها أنها كانت متجددة في الزمان الأول ثم في الزمان الثاني صارت غير متجددة، فقد صارت غير متجددة بعد أن كانت موصوفة بأنها متجددة فيلزم أن يكون حدوثها وتجددها صفة زائدة على ذاتها، وهذا محال ؛ لأنه لو كان الحدوث صفة زائدة لكانت تلك الصفة حادثة، ويلزم التسلسل.
The eighteenth issue: On God's eternity (baqa'). The discourse on it is arranged in two chapters: The first chapter: On the reality of eternity. Know that a thing, when it was non-existent then came into existence, its existence in the first moment is origination (huduth), and then its existence after that is eternity (baqa'). Most of the verifiers agreed that origination cannot be an attribute additional to the essence of the originated. As for eternity, they differed as to whether it is additional to the essence of the eternal or not. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr and Imam al-Haramayn (from our companions) and the majority of the Basran Mu'tazila held that the thing's being eternal is not an attribute additional to the essence. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and most of his followers and the majority of the Baghdadi Mu'tazila held that it is an attribute additional to the essence. And know that in this issue there are three investigations: The first investigation: Whether the continuance of the essence is an additional concept to the essence or not? Some said: It is an additional concept to the essence; because the essence was present in the first moment, and the continuance of the essence did not exist in the first moment. When it came to be in the second moment, the essence came to be and the continuance of the essence came to be, and this necessitates that the continuance of the essence is other than the essence itself. But this statement has an objection: Whenever it is true of the essence that it has become continuous after not having been so, it is true of it that it was renewing (mutajaddid) in the first moment, then in the second moment it became non-renewing. So it became non-renewing after it was described as renewing. This necessitates that its origination and renewal (huduth and tajaddud) be attributes additional to its essence. And this is impossible; because if origination were an additional attribute, that attribute would be originated, leading to infinite regress.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage begins the eighteenth issue (mas'ala) of the work, on God's eternity (baqa'). The author announces that the discussion is organized into two chapters (fasl). The first chapter is on the reality of baqa'. Imam Razi defines huduth (origination) as the existence of a thing when it was non-existent, and baqa' (eternity/continuance) as its existence after that. He notes that scholars agreed that huduth is not an additional attribute (since it is the very fact of coming into existence, not a separate quality). However, they differed on baqa': is it an additional attribute or not? He lists two positions: the first group (Qadi Abu Bakr, Imam al-Haramayn from the Ash'aris, and most Basran Mu'tazila) says baqa' is not additional; the second group (Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, most of his followers, and most Baghdadi Mu'tazila) says it is additional. Then the author states that there are three investigations (abhath) in this issue. He presents the first investigation: whether the continuance (istimrar) of the essence is an additional concept. Some argue it is additional: in the first moment, the essence existed but its continuance did not; in the second moment, both exist, so continuance must be other than the essence. Then an objection (ishkal) is raised: if we say the essence 'became continuous' after not being continuous, then we must say it was 'renewing' (mutajaddid) in the first moment, and in the second moment it became 'non-renewing'. This would require that 'origination' and 'renewal' themselves are attributes additional to the essence, which is impossible because it would lead to infinite regress. The passage ends with this objection waiting for an answer.

Key Terms
استمرار
مفهوم زائد
تجدد
تسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the argument for continuance being additional is sound and leads to the correct view.
Correction: Razi presents a strong objection showing that the argument leads to an infinite regress, thus the argument is flawed.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of accepting the argument that continuance is an additional concept, according to the objection?
A) It proves God's eternity
B) It leads to infinite regress
C) It contradicts the Quran
D) It is accepted by all scholars

Key Takeaway
The first investigation shows that claiming continuance (istimrar) is an additional attribute leads to an unacceptable infinite regress, indicating the argument is not sound.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi shows that adding a concept like 'continuance' to Allah's essence leads to an absurd infinite regress. Where in your own understanding of Allah's attributes might you be adding concepts that are not strictly from revelation? What will you do to correct this?
?
The objection reveals that flawed reasoning about Allah can lead to contradictions. Have you ever accepted a belief about Allah without properly examining its logical implications? How will you ensure your aqeedah is sound both textually and rationally?
?
Infinite regress is impossible in divine matters. Does your heart ever imagine Allah's actions or attributes as a chain of causes (e.g., 'why did He create?'). How does this lesson call you to purify your tawheed from such subtle errors?

The Definition of Baqa and the Disagreement on Its Nature
Razi defines baqa and states the two views on whether it is an additional attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of baqa as the continuation of existence after origination and the two conflicting views on whether baqa is an additional attribute.

Core Idea
Baqa is the persistence of existence; scholars disagree if it adds something to the essence.

In this passage, Imam Razi lays the foundation for discussing God's attribute of baqa. He first defines baqa in relation to huduth (origination), then presents the two main schools of thought on whether baqa is an attribute superadded to the essence. This sets the stage for the arguments that follow in subsequent chapters.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the English translation. Let the author's own terms and structure come through.
Notice the contrast between huduth and baqa right from the start.
2
Understand the definition
Focus on how Razi defines baqa: existence after the first moment. This is the conceptual foundation for the whole discussion.
3
Identify the two positions
Find the two groups of scholars and what each believes: one says baqa is not additional, the other says it is.
List the names mentioned: al-Qadi Abu Bakr, Imam al-Haramayn, Basran Mu'tazilites vs. al-Ash'ari, his followers, Baghdad Mu'tazilites.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why does this disagreement matter for understanding divine attributes? The commentary will help connect the dots.
This prepares you for the proofs that come later in the chapter.

المسألة الثامنة عشرة في بقاء الله تعالى والكلام فيه مرتب على فصلين : الفصل الأول : في حقيقة البقاء اعلم أن الشيء إذا كان معدوماً ثم صار موجودًا فوجوده في الزمان الأول هو الحدوث، ثم وجوده في الذي بعد ذلك هو البقاء. وأكثر المحققين اتفقوا على أن الحدوث لا يمكن أن يكون صفة زائدة على ذات الحادث، وأما البقاء فقد اختلفوا في أنه هل هو زائد على ذات الباقي أن لا؟ فذهب القاضي أبو بكر وإمام الحرمين - من أصحابنا - وجمهور معتزلة البصرة إلى أن كون الباقي باقيا ليس صفة زائدة على الذات وذهب الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري وأكثر أتباعه وجمهور معتزلة بغدادي إلى أنه صفة زائدة على الذات.
The eighteenth question concerning the eternity (baqa) of God, may He be exalted. The discussion on it is arranged in two chapters: The first chapter: on the reality of baqa. Know that when a thing was non-existent and then came into existence, its existence in the first moment is origination (huduth), and its existence in what follows that is baqa. The majority of the investigators agreed that huduth cannot be an attribute superadded to the essence of the originated thing. As for baqa, they differed as to whether it is superadded to the essence of that which persists (al-baqi) or not. Al-Qadi Abu Bakr, Imam al-Haramayn – from our companions – and the majority of the Basran Mu'tazilites held that the fact that that which persists is persisting (kawn al-baqi baqiyan) is not an attribute superadded to the essence. And Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, most of his followers, and the majority of the Baghdad Mu'tazilites held that it is an attribute superadded to the essence.
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage defines the term baqa and outlines the main disagreement regarding its ontological status. Razi begins by defining baqa in relation to huduth: if something comes into existence, its existence at the first moment is huduth, and its existence in subsequent moments is baqa. This sets up the question of whether baqa is an additional property or not. He notes that all investigators agree huduth is not an additional attribute, but baqa is disputed. He then names the two schools: (1) Abu Bakr al-Baqillani, Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, and the Basran Mu'tazilites hold that baqa is not an attribute added to the essence; (2) Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, most Ash'arites, and the Baghdad Mu'tazilites hold that it is an added attribute. This prepares the reader for the subsequent investigations into the nature of baqa.

Correction: Baqa is explicitly defined as existence after the first moment, so it is distinct from huduth, which is existence at the first moment.
